## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / constitutive modeling of materials (thermo-mechanical stress–strain behavior)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is the core setting of thermoelasticity and temperature-dependent plasticity in materials science. Common relationships include elastic laws with temperature-dependent modulus, thermal expansion offsets, and plastic/strain-hardening laws with thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear elasticity (Hooke): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime, constant modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linearized E(T) effect on elastic slope)
- Reciprocal modulus softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (T + c1) (elastic stiffness decreases with T)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain)
- Thermoelastic with E(T) and alpha(T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - (c2 + c3 * T) * (T - c4)) (combined temperature effects on modulus and thermal strain)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate strain nonlinearity without explicit plasticity)
- Exponential strain stiffening (hyperelastic-like): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (rapid stiffening at larger strains)
- Hollomon power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 * exp(-c1 * T)) * epsilon**c2 (plastic strain hardening with temperature-reduced strength)
- Ramberg–Osgood (inverted-style stress law): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear compliance; useful empirical fit)
- Voce hardening with temperature-dependent saturation: sigma = (c0 * exp(-c1 * T)) + (c2 * exp(-c3 * T)) * (1 - exp(-(c4 * exp(-c5 * T)) * epsilon)) (saturating hardening and thermal softening)
- Thermal-softening factorized form: sigma = f(epsilon) * (1 - (c0 * T)**c1) (strength decreases toward a critical/high temperature; common in phenomenological models)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic proxy (smooth blend): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (1 + exp(c2 * (epsilon - (c3 + c4 * T)))) + (c5 * exp(-c6 * T)) * epsilon**c7 (elastic branch transitioning to plastic hardening with T-dependent yield-like strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic slope identification: near epsilon ≈ 0, sigma ≈ E(T) * epsilon; look for models linear in epsilon with E varying smoothly with T (often decreasing with T).
- Thermal expansion offset: if sigma crosses zero at nonzero epsilon and the zero-stress strain shifts with T, include an (epsilon - alpha*(T - T0)) structure.
- Thermal softening separability: many metals/polymer strengths approximately factor as sigma ≈ g(epsilon) * h(T); try multiplicative temperature factors like exp(-c*T) or 1 - (c*T)^m.
- Hardening saturation: if d(sigma)/d(epsilon) decreases with increasing epsilon, use saturating forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) rather than pure power laws.
- Strain stiffening vs softening: convex-up sigma(epsilon) suggests exponential or high-order polynomial terms; concave-down suggests power-law with exponent < 1 or Voce-type saturation.
- Yield/transition behavior: a distinct change in slope vs epsilon (especially varying with T) suggests a smooth-switch or rational blend between elastic and plastic terms.
- Temperature-shifting yield point: if the strain at which nonlinearity starts moves with T, make the transition strain (or yield-like parameter) depend on T (e.g., c0 + c1*T).
- Stability/physical constraints: enforce sigma(0, T) ≈ 0 for purely mechanical loading by avoiding standalone constant terms unless modeling residual/thermal stress.
- Sign handling: if epsilon can be tensile/compressive, use odd-in-epsilon structures (linear + cubic) or include Abs(epsilon) only inside magnitude terms to keep sigma sign consistent.

GT: -c0*(T - c1) + epsilon*c2*exp(-(T - c3)**c4)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):  
\[
-0.6056800229\,(T-298.0016449)\;+\;\epsilon\cdot 3.1473717381\cdot \exp\!\big(-(T-298.0016449)^2\big)
\]
Key structural facts:
- As a function of **T**, it is **linear** plus a **Gaussian bump in T** multiplied by **ε**.
- As a function of **ε**, it is **exactly affine**: \(A(T)+\epsilon\,B(T)\). No \(\epsilon^2,\epsilon^3,\exp(\epsilon),\log(\epsilon),|\epsilon|\), etc.
- The ε-dependent coefficient is \(B(T)=3.1473\exp(-(T-298.0016)^2)\), i.e., depends on **T via \(\exp(-(\text{shifted }T)^2)\)**, not via cos/sin/log/rational.

So any candidate must be able (after choosing constants, possibly zeroing terms) to become:
- a linear function in T (from the \(-0.60568(T-298...)\) part), **plus**
- an ε-term whose coefficient is a Gaussian in shifted T.

Now check candidates.

1) Has \(\log(Tc3+1)\), \(\cos(Tc9)\), and \(\exp(c2|\epsilon|)\) etc. ε appears inside exponent/abs/log → not affine in ε. Cannot match.

2) \(T c0 + c1 e^{c2\epsilon} + c3\epsilon^3 + c8\epsilon^2 + \dots\). To be affine in ε, must kill \(\epsilon^2,\epsilon^3\) (set c3=c8=0) and kill \(e^{c2\epsilon}\) dependence (either c1=0 or c2=0 making it constant). Then remaining ε-dependence is none (unless cosine term kept, but that gives \(e^{c6\epsilon}\) etc). No way to get \(\epsilon\cdot e^{-(T-\mu)^2}\). Cannot.

3) Similar: only ε appears in \(e^{c2\epsilon}\) and \(e^{c6\epsilon}\). No linear ε term with Gaussian-in-T coefficient. Cannot.

4) Has linear ε terms \(c3\epsilon + c8\epsilon\), good, but the ε-coefficient would be constant (sum of constants), not \(e^{-(T-\mu)^2}\). Other ε dependence is via \(e^{c6\epsilon}\) in cosine term (non-affine unless killed). If kill cosine term and exponentials, ε coefficient is constant → cannot match GT’s \(B(T)\) varying with T. Cannot.

5) No linear ε term at all (only \(e^{c3\epsilon}\), \(e^{c6\epsilon}\), etc). Cannot.

6) Has \(c3\epsilon\) but also \(\epsilon^2\) and exponentials in ε unless killed. If kill non-affine parts, ε coefficient becomes constant, not Gaussian in T. Cannot.

7) ε appears in \(e^{c2\epsilon}\), \(e^{c5\epsilon}\), and \(\epsilon^{1/3}e^{Tc8}\) (nonlinear). Cannot.

8) Only ε in exponentials \(e^{c2\epsilon}, e^{c5\epsilon}\). Cannot.

9) Only ε in exponentials. Cannot.

10) Polynomial ε^2, ε^3, ε^4 plus exponentials. Cannot become exactly affine in ε while also producing Gaussian-in-T coefficient. Cannot.

11) Has linear ε terms (several), plus \(e^{c5\epsilon}\cos(Tc6)\) (non-affine unless c4=0). If set c4=0, ε coefficient is constant again. No Gaussian-in-T coefficient. Cannot.

12) Only ε in \(e^{c2\epsilon}\) and \(e^{c6\epsilon}\). Cannot.

13) Has a linear ε term \(c9\epsilon\), but no way to make its coefficient depend on T as Gaussian; other T-dependence is cosines. Cannot.

14) Has ε^2 and ε^3; even if set c7=0 and try to remove ε^3 (but ε^3 has fixed coefficient 1, cannot be removed). So cannot be affine in ε. Cannot.

15) Only ε in exponentials. Cannot.

16) Has \(\log(c4\epsilon+1)\) and exponentials in ε. Not affine in ε. Cannot.

17) Has linear ε terms \(c3\epsilon + c7\epsilon\). If kill cosine exponential term (c5=0) and kill \(e^{c2\epsilon}\) by c1=0 or c2=0, then ε coefficient is constant. Not Gaussian in T. Cannot.

18) Same issue plus ε^2 term. If set c7=0, still constant ε coefficient. Cannot.

19) ε appears only in \(e^{c2\epsilon}\), \(e^{c5\epsilon}\), and \(\epsilon/(T+c8)\) (affine in ε but coefficient is \(1/(T+c8)\), not Gaussian). No way to turn \(1/(T+c8)\) into \(e^{-(T-\mu)^2}\) on any plausible continuous domain (they are different analytic forms; cannot be identical on an interval). Cannot.

20) Only ε in exponentials. Cannot.

21) ε appears inside \(\log(c6|\epsilon|+1)\) multiplied by cos(T). Not affine in ε. Cannot.

22) Has linear ε and ε^2. If set c7=0 and kill exp*cos term, ε coefficient constant. Not Gaussian. Cannot.

23) Only ε in exponentials. Cannot.

24) Only ε in exponentials. Cannot.

25) Has ε^3 term; can set its coefficient c3=0, but still only ε in exponentials/cos unless killed; no linear ε with Gaussian-in-T coefficient. Cannot.

26) Has linear ε term \(c1\epsilon\), but other ε dependence is \(e^{c3\epsilon}\) and \(e^{c6\epsilon}\) unless killed. If kill them, ε coefficient constant. Not Gaussian. Cannot.

27) ε appears in \(\epsilon\log(Tc1+1)\), \(\log(c4\epsilon+1)\), and \(\sin(c7\epsilon+c8)\). Not affine in ε. Even if kill nonlinear terms, remaining ε coefficient is \(\log(Tc1+1)+c5\), not Gaussian. Cannot.

28) Polynomial in ε (ε, ε^2, ε^3) and sin in T. GT is affine in ε and Gaussian in T. Cannot.

29) Has \(|T+\epsilon|\) (mixing T and ε) and ε/(T+c6) and exp*cos. Not affine in ε globally; could assume domain where \(T+\epsilon\ge 0\) to drop Abs, but still gives a term \(c3(T+\epsilon)\) which makes ε coefficient constant and also adds extra T term; still no Gaussian-in-T coefficient. Cannot.

30) Has extra \(e^{Tc8}\log(|\epsilon|)\) type term; not affine in ε. Cannot.

31) Only ε in exponentials. Cannot.

32) Has \(|T+\epsilon|\) and ε/(T+c9). Even with domain to remove Abs, ε coefficient becomes constant plus rational in T, not Gaussian. Cannot.

33) Has linear ε term \((c7+1)\epsilon\) (note extra “+ epsilon” fixed). Coefficient is constant, not Gaussian in T. Other ε dependence only via \(e^{c2\epsilon}\) etc unless killed. Cannot.

34) Has \(\log(Tc2+1)\log(c3\epsilon+1)\) and \( \epsilon e^{c7/T}|\epsilon|^{c8}\). Not affine in ε. Cannot.

35) No linear ε term at all; only \(e^{c2\epsilon}\). Cannot.

36) Has \(e^{Tc5}\) and \(\sin(c7+c8\epsilon)\). Not affine in ε. Cannot.

37) No ε at all. Cannot.

38) Linear and polynomial ε terms; also sin in T. Cannot produce ε*Gaussian(T). Cannot.

39) Has \(1/(c7\epsilon+c8)\) (non-affine). Cannot.

40) ε appears in \(\epsilon e^{c2|\epsilon|}\log(Tc3+1)\) and rational in \(|\epsilon|^{c8}\). Not affine in ε. Cannot.

41) Has \(T c0 \epsilon e^{c1|\epsilon|}\) etc. Not affine in ε. Cannot.

42) Has rational \(c4/(c5\epsilon+c6)\) and exp*cos. Not affine in ε. Cannot.

43) Has exp(ε) terms and a linear ε term \(c9\epsilon\) with constant coefficient. No Gaussian-in-T coefficient. Cannot.

44) Has ε/(T+c8) plus cos(T) and exp(ε). Not Gaussian. Cannot.

45) Has \(|T+\epsilon|\) and ε/(T+c8). Even with domain removing Abs, still wrong T-dependence for ε coefficient. Cannot.

46) Has ε/(T+c6)^5 and cos(T) and exp(ε). Not Gaussian. Cannot.

47) ε log(Tc1+1) etc and log(ε+1) and rational in |ε|. Not affine. Cannot.

48) ε multiplied by \(e^{c2|\epsilon|}\log(Tc3+1)\) plus \(e^{c5\epsilon}\). Not affine. Cannot.

49) Same plus ε/(T+c7)^5. Not affine. Cannot.

50) Only ε in exponentials. Cannot.

Conclusion: none of the candidates can generate the essential GT structure \(\epsilon\cdot K\cdot \exp(-(T-\mu)^2)\) while also keeping exact affine dependence in ε and linear-in-T baseline (up to a constant shift). No candidate contains a Gaussian in shifted T at all; the only T-nonlinearities present are trig, log, rational, or \(e^{aT}\), which cannot be made identical to \(e^{-(T-\mu)^2}\) on any nontrivial continuous domain by parameter choice.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.6057*(T - 298.00) + epsilon*3.1474*exp(-(T - 298.00)²)`

Expanding: `-0.6057*T + 0.6057*298.00 + epsilon*3.1474*exp(-(T-298)²)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. A linear term in T
2. A constant term
3. `epsilon * exp(-(T-298)²)` — this is epsilon times a Gaussian in T

The key feature is the `epsilon * exp(-(T-298)²)` term. This is a Gaussian function of T multiplied by epsilon. Let me check if any candidate can produce this.

Note: `exp(-(T-298)²)` is NOT expressible as products of `exp(f(epsilon))` and `cos(g(T))` or similar. The Gaussian in T is a fundamentally different basis function from `cos(T)`, `sin(T)`, `exp(epsilon)*cos(T)`, etc.

Let me examine the candidates systematically. Most candidates contain terms like `exp(c*epsilon)*cos(T*c)` or `cos(T)` or `sin(T*c+c)`. None of these can produce `epsilon*exp(-T²)` type behavior.

**Key observation:** The GT's epsilon-dependent term is `epsilon * exp(-(T-298)²)`. This requires a Gaussian in T. None of the candidates contain `exp(-T²)` or `exp(T²)` type terms. They contain:
- `exp(c*epsilon)` — exponential in epsilon, not T
- `cos(T*c)`, `sin(T*c)` — trigonometric in T
- `log(T*c+1)` — logarithmic in T
- `exp(T*c)` — exponential in T (not Gaussian)
- `epsilon*exp(c*|epsilon|)*log(T*c+1)` — not Gaussian in T

A Gaussian `exp(-T²)` cannot be expressed as any finite combination of `exp(T)`, `cos(T)`, `sin(T)`, `log(T)`, polynomials in T, etc. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

Let me verify each candidate cannot match:

**Candidates 1-50:** Every single candidate uses combinations of `exp(c*epsilon)`, `cos(T*c)`, `sin(T*c+c)`, `log(T*c+1)`, `exp(T*c)`, polynomial terms in epsilon, `epsilon/(T+c)`, `|T+epsilon|`, etc. None contain `exp(-T²)` or any equivalent Gaussian-in-T term.

Since `epsilon*exp(-(T-298)²)` requires a Gaussian in T, and no candidate has this basis function, none can match.
